10	
11	Tony's primary use for HerdrPlus is **agent orchestration** — an orchestrator (external to herdrplus OR an agent inside a herdrplus pane) driving one or more agent terminals: creating workspaces, tabs, panes, and running agent CLIs in them.
12	
13	**Driving agents in panes (learned this session):**
14	- Launch an agent CLI in a pane: `herdrplus pane run <pane_id> "<cli>"`. CLIs available on this box: `grok` (Grok 4.5), `agy` (Antigravity/Gemini). `grok` rate-limits fast.
15	- **Agy YOLO / auto-approve:** `agy --continue --dangerously-skip-permissions` (resumes prior conversation + skips all permission gates). Without it, agy stops at every tool-permission prompt — its menus are ARROW-driven (send-keys down/enter), NOT number-driven.
16	- These CLI agents **stop at turn boundaries even in auto-approve mode** — the orchestrator must prod them to continue with specific instructions. They do not run to completion unattended.
17	- **Monitor via git ground-truth, not screen scraping.** `pane read` retained-buffer text false-matches on stale output (e.g. old "WS1-DONE"). Poll for the actual commit/file on disk instead. A status board that classifies each pane BUSY/IDLE/BLOCKED(dep)/DONE by cross-referencing pane output + git deliverable + dependency readiness beats a single blocking watcher.
18	- **Feedback (why):** Tony called out twice that all agents run async and I should watch ALL of them continuously without waiting on one, and without a fixed timer — check state constantly, act on whichever is actionable. **How to apply:** never serialize on one agent's watcher; poll all panes' state each cycle, prod idle-with-dep-ready agents immediately, never let an agent set its own wait-timer.
19	
20	**Build/binary note:** a running `herdrplus.exe` LOCKS the binary — must kill all herdrplus/herdr processes before a release build or the linker can't overwrite the exe (symptom: rebuild "succeeds" but old binary persists). See [[herdr-windows-build]].
21

10	herdr (cloned at `K:\Downloads\__Projects.Mine\herdr4Windows\__references\herdr`, upstream ogulcancelik/herdr, master) builds on Windows with a plain `cargo build --release` — all required setup lives in `K:\Downloads\__Projects.Mine\herdr4Windows\.cargo\config.toml` (ancestor config, keeps the clone clean):
11	
12	- `[build] target-dir` → `__solutions/target` (user wants ALL build output in `__solutions`)
13	- `[env]` sets `ZIG = C:/Zig/zig.exe` (Zig 0.15.2, installed 2026-07-17) and `ZIG_GLOBAL_CACHE_DIR = K:/.../.zig-global-cache`
14	
15	**Why:** `build.rs` compiles vendored `libghostty-vt` via `zig build` (min zig 0.15.2). Zig's default global cache is on `C:` while the project is on `K:`; Windows can't relativize cross-drive paths, so Zig panics with `Run.zig:662 assert(!std.fs.path.isAbsolute(...))`. Same-drive cache fixes it.
16	
17	**How to apply:** Just `cargo build --release` from inside the project tree — do not delete `.cargo/config.toml`. Toolchain pinned via rust-toolchain.toml to 1.96.1 (rustup auto-installs). Output: `__solutions\target\release\herdrplus.exe` (~17 MB; bin renamed from herdr.exe 2026-07-18 via `[[bin]]`, package name still `herdr`, tests run as `cargo test --bin herdrplus`). No lib target — never use `cargo test --lib`. Never set HERDR_UPDATE_API_SCHEMA casually: it's in build.rs rerun-if-env-changed and forces a ~5-10 min full rebuild.

# Brainstorming Ideas Into Designs

Help turn ideas into fully formed designs and specs through natural collaborative dialogue.

Start by understanding the current project context, then ask questions one at a time to refine the idea. Once you understand what you're building, present the design and get user approval.

<HARD-GATE>
Do NOT invoke any implementation skill, write any code, scaffold any project, or take any implementation action until you have presented a design and the user has approved it. This applies to EVERY project regardless of perceived simplicity.
</HARD-GATE>

## Anti-Pattern: "This Is Too Simple To Need A Design"

Every project goes through this process. A todo list, a single-function utility, a config change — all of them. "Simple" projects are where unexamined assumptions cause the most wasted work. The design can be short (a few sentences for truly simple projects), but you MUST present it and get approval.

## Checklist

You MUST create a task for each of these items and complete them in order:

1. **Explore project context** — check files, docs, recent commits
2. **Offer the visual companion just-in-time** — NOT upfront. The first time a question would genuinely be clearer shown than described, offer it then (its own message); on approval its browser tab opens for you. If no visual question ever arises, never offer it. See the Visual Companion section below.
3. **Ask clarifying questions** — one at a time, understand purpose/constraints/success criteria
4. **Propose 2-3 approaches** — with trade-offs and your recommendation
5. **Present design** — in sections scaled to their complexity, get user approval after each section
6. **Write design doc** — save to `docs/superpowers/specs/YYYY-MM-DD-<topic>-design.md` and commit
7. **Spec self-review** — quick inline check for placeholders, contradictions, ambiguity, scope (see below)
8. **User reviews written spec** — ask user to review the spec file before proceeding
9. **Transition to implementation** — invoke writing-plans skill to create implementation plan

## Process Flow

```dot
digraph brainstorming {
    "Explore project context" [shape=box];
    "Ask clarifying questions" [shape=box];
    "Propose 2-3 approaches" [shape=box];
    "Present design sections" [shape=box];
    "User approves design?" [shape=diamond];
    "Write design doc" [shape=box];
    "Spec self-review\n(fix inline)" [shape=box];
    "User reviews spec?" [shape=diamond];
    "Invoke writing-plans skill" [shape=doublecircle];

    "Explore project context" -> "Ask clarifying questions";
    "Ask clarifying questions" -> "Propose 2-3 approaches";
    "Propose 2-3 approaches" -> "Present design sections";
    "Present design sections" -> "User approves design?";
    "User approves design?" -> "Present design sections" [label="no, revise"];
    "User approves design?" -> "Write design doc" [label="yes"];
    "Write design doc" -> "Spec self-review\n(fix inline)";
    "Spec self-review\n(fix inline)" -> "User reviews spec?";
    "User reviews spec?" -> "Write design doc" [label="changes requested"];
    "User reviews spec?" -> "Invoke writing-plans skill" [label="approved"];
}
```

**The terminal state is invoking writing-plans.** Do NOT invoke frontend-design, mcp-builder, or any other implementation skill. The ONLY skill you invoke after brainstorming is writing-plans.

## The Process

**Understanding the idea:**

- Check out the current project state first (files, docs, recent commits)
- Before asking detailed questions, assess scope: if the request describes multiple independent subsystems (e.g., "build a platform with chat, file storage, billing, and analytics"), flag this immediately. Don't spend questions refining details of a project that needs to be decomposed first.
- If the project is too large for a single spec, help the user decompose into sub-projects: what are the independent pieces, how do they relate, what order should they be built? Then brainstorm the first sub-project through the normal design flow. Each sub-project gets its own spec → plan → implementation cycle.
- For appropriately-scoped projects, ask questions one at a time to refine the idea
- Prefer multiple choice questions when possible, but open-ended is fine too
- Only one question per message - if a topic needs more exploration, break it into multiple questions
- Focus on understanding: purpose, constraints, success criteria

**Exploring approaches:**

- Propose 2-3 different approaches with trade-offs
- Present options conversationally with your recommendation and reasoning
- Lead with your recommended option and explain why

**Presenting the design:**

- Once you believe you understand what you're building, present the design
- Scale each section to its complexity: a few sentences if straightforward, up to 200-300 words if nuanced
- Ask after each section whether it looks right so far
- Cover: architecture, components, data flow, error handling, testing
- Be ready to go back and clarify if something doesn't make sense

**Design for isolation and clarity:**

- Break the system into smaller units that each have one clear purpose, communicate through well-defined interfaces, and can be understood and tested independently
- For each unit, you should be able to answer: what does it do, how do you use it, and what does it depend on?
- Can someone understand what a unit does without reading its internals? Can you change the internals without breaking consumers? If not, the boundaries need work.
- Smaller, well-bounded units are also easier for you to work with - you reason better about code you can hold in context at once, and your edits are more reliable when files are focused. When a file grows large, that's often a signal that it's doing too much.

**Working in existing codebases:**

- Explore the current structure before proposing changes. Follow existing patterns.
- Where existing code has problems that affect the work (e.g., a file that's grown too large, unclear boundaries, tangled responsibilities), include targeted improvements as part of the design - the way a good developer improves code they're working in.
- Don't propose unrelated refactoring. Stay focused on what serves the current goal.

## After the Design

**Documentation:**

- Write the validated design (spec) to `docs/superpowers/specs/YYYY-MM-DD-<topic>-design.md`
  - (User preferences for spec location override this default)
- Use elements-of-style:writing-clearly-and-concisely skill if available
- Commit the design document to git

**Spec Self-Review:**
After writing the spec document, look at it with fresh eyes:

1. **Placeholder scan:** Any "TBD", "TODO", incomplete sections, or vague requirements? Fix them.
2. **Internal consistency:** Do any sections contradict each other? Does the architecture match the feature descriptions?
3. **Scope check:** Is this focused enough for a single implementation plan, or does it need decomposition?
4. **Ambiguity check:** Could any requirement be interpreted two different ways? If so, pick one and make it explicit.

Fix any issues inline. No need to re-review — just fix and move on.

**User Review Gate:**
After the spec review loop passes, ask the user to review the written spec before proceeding:

> "Spec written and committed to `<path>`. Please review it and let me know if you want to make any changes before we start writing out the implementation plan."

Wait for the user's response. If they request changes, make them and re-run the spec review loop. Only proceed once the user approves.

**Implementation:**

- Invoke the writing-plans skill to create a detailed implementation plan
- Do NOT invoke any other skill. writing-plans is the next step.

## Key Principles

- **One question at a time** - Don't overwhelm with multiple questions
- **Multiple choice preferred** - Easier to answer than open-ended when possible
- **YAGNI ruthlessly** - Remove unnecessary features from all designs
- **Explore alternatives** - Always propose 2-3 approaches before settling
- **Incremental validation** - Present design, get approval before moving on
- **Be flexible** - Go back and clarify when something doesn't make sense

## Visual Companion

A browser-based companion for showing mockups, diagrams, and visual options during brainstorming. Available as a tool — not a mode. Accepting the companion means it's available for questions that benefit from visual treatment; it does NOT mean every question goes through the browser.

**Offering the companion (just-in-time):** Do NOT offer it upfront. Wait until a question would genuinely be clearer shown than told — a real mockup / layout / diagram question, not merely a UI *topic*. The first time that happens, offer it then, as its own message:
> "This next part might be easier if I show you — I can put together mockups, diagrams, and comparisons in a browser tab as we go. It's still new and can be token-intensive. Want me to? I'll open it for you."

**This offer MUST be its own message.** Only the offer — no clarifying question, summary, or other content. Wait for the user's response. If they accept, start the server with `--open` so their browser opens to the first screen automatically. If they decline, continue text-only and don't offer again unless they raise it.

**Per-question decision:** Even after the user accepts, decide FOR EACH QUESTION whether to use the browser or the terminal. The test: **would the user understand this better by seeing it than reading it?**

- **Use the browser** for content that IS visual — mockups, wireframes, layout comparisons, architecture diagrams, side-by-side visual designs
- **Use the terminal** for content that is text — requirements questions, conceptual choices, tradeoff lists, A/B/C/D text options, scope decisions

A question about a UI topic is not automatically a visual question. "What does personality mean in this context?" is a conceptual question — use the terminal. "Which wizard layout works better?" is a visual question — use the browser.

If they agree to the companion, read the detailed guide before proceeding:
`skills/brainstorming/visual-companion.md`

--- ASSISTANT [2026-07-18T20:06:00.522Z] ---
Now the architectural fork — where does the spawn logic live? Three options:

**A. Server-native `team.spawn` wire method (my recommendation).** One request; the server creates the workspace, splits/labels the N panes, launches each command, joins them to the group, balances the layout, and returns the pane map. Protocol bumps to 19.
- *For:* This is the precedent — pane balance and msg bus are both server-native. It's the only option where partial failure is handled in one place with full authority (server can roll back the workspace if pane 3 of 5 fails to spawn). Group membership is wired up inside the same code that owns msg teardown — the exact lifecycle-edge territory where Sol56 found bugs last time, so keeping it in one owner matters. And a future TUI keybind or command palette entry gets it for free.
- *Against:* Protocol bump ceremony (wire.rs, schema regen, 3 test files), and the server grows a mini-orchestrator.

**B. Client-side composition.** `team spawn` is CLI sugar issuing existing wire calls in sequence (workspace.create → pane.split ×N → rename → run → group join → balance).
- *For:* Zero protocol/server changes; every primitive already exists and is tested.
- *Against:* Partial failure leaves a half-built workspace the client must clean up over the wire (racy if the client dies mid-spawn); the agent registry has to be resolved client-side even though the server owns config; nothing else (TUI) can reuse it.

**C. B now, promote to A later.** Ship sugar fast, migrate when the TUI wants it.
- *Against:* We'd pay the migration cost on top, and the failure-cleanup code written for B gets thrown away.

I recommend **A**. The one-shot atomicity and correct group lifecycle are the actual point of the feature, and both are server-side concerns. `--wait` stays client-side in all variants (CLI polls pane agent-state via existing reads), so the server addition stays bounded.

Agree with A, or want to talk through one of the others?

--- ASSISTANT [2026-07-18T20:58:01.699Z] ---
Grounding done — two useful facts: `pane run` is just `PaneSendInput` (types the command into the pane's shell + Enter), and the API already exposes `PaneAgentState` per pane, which gives `--wait` something to poll. Now the design, in sections.

## Section 1: CLI surface

```
herdrplus team spawn <team-name>
    --agents <entry>[,<entry>...]     # entry = agent | label=agent
    [--cwd <dir>]                     # shared by all panes; default: caller's cwd
    [--with-orch [cmd]]               # extra pane labeled "orch"; default cmd = plain shell
    [--wait] [--timeout <secs>]       # poll until all agent panes ready
    [--json]                          # machine-readable pane map (default for non-tty)
```

- `<team-name>` becomes both the **workspace label** and the **msg group name**. Example: `herdrplus team spawn review --agents ws1=claude,ws2=claude,reviewer=grok --wait`.
- Label defaults: `claude-1`, `claude-2`, `grok-1` (per-agent counters). Duplicate explicit labels are an error at parse time, before anything is created.
- Output: pane map `{workspace_id, group, panes: [{label, pane_id, agent, command}]}` — exactly what an orchestrator needs to start `msg send`-ing.
- Companion subcommand for later sessions: `team status <name>` is **out of scope** for v1 (existing `pane list` + `msg who` cover it); teardown is `workspace close` (msg teardown on workspace close already handles group cleanup — shipped in PR #2).

## Section 2: Agent registry (config)

New optional config section:

```toml
[team.agents]
claude = "claude --dangerously-skip-permissions"
agy    = "agy --continue --dangerously-skip-permissions"
grok   = "grok"
```

- Resolution happens **server-side** (server owns config, consistent with everything else). Roster name → registry lookup → hit: use configured command string; miss: the name itself is the command, verbatim (so `--agents "ws1=pwsh -NoLogo"` works with quoting).
- The registry value is a full command line typed into the pane's shell (same mechanism as `pane run`), so anything launchable from a shell works — no argv parsing needed by us.

## Section 3: Wire method

- `team.spawn` — protocol **19** (strict-equality gate; full bump checklist from memory: `wire.rs`, schema regen, `api_ping.rs`, `cli_wrapper.rs`, `tests/support/mod.rs`).
- Params: `{name, entries: [{label?, agent}], cwd?, orch_command??, focus?}`. Result: the pane map above.
- Server-side sequence (one handler, owns rollback): create workspace → split to N (+orch) panes → set pane labels → join each to group `<name>` → send each pane its command text → apply `layout.balance` (reuse PR #1 logic) → return map.
- **Rollback:** if any step fails, close the workspace (which cascades pane + group teardown through the already-hardened msg teardown path) and return one error naming the failed step. No half-built teams.
- `--wait` stays client-side: CLI polls `pane get`/`pane list` agent state until every agent pane leaves `unknown`/startup, or timeout → exit code distinct from spawn failure, with per-pane status in the error output.

Does this look right so far? Sections still to come: data flow/ordering details, error handling specifics, and testing.

--- ASSISTANT [2026-07-18T22:32:43.892Z] ---
Yes. The installed Grok CLI has a YOLO equivalent — actually two ways to get there:

- `--always-approve` — auto-approve all tool executions
- `--permission-mode bypassPermissions` (or the softer `dontAsk`)

It also has `-c/--continue` for resuming the cwd's last session, same shape as agy's. So a sensible registry default for your config would be:

```toml
[team.agents]
grok = "grok --always-approve"
# or the resume-style variant, mirroring agy:
# grok = "grok --continue --always-approve"
```

One bonus finding while I had the help open: grok has `--worktree` built in — it can put its own session in a fresh git worktree per agent. That means the "worktree per agent" protection we deferred out of team-spawn v1 is already reachable today purely via registry config (`grok = "grok --worktree --always-approve"`), no herdrplus feature needed. Supports keeping v1 to a single shared `--cwd`.

Back to the design when you're ready — Sections 1–3 (CLI surface, agent registry, wire method) are awaiting your look; data flow, error handling, and testing sections still to come.

--- ASSISTANT [2026-07-18T22:35:46.482Z] ---
Sections 1–3 approved. Here are the remaining sections.

## Section 4: Data flow / ordering

Server handler for `team.spawn`, in order:

1. **Resolve** every roster entry against `[team.agents]` (miss → entry is the command verbatim). Any resolution problem fails before anything is created.
2. **Create workspace** (label = team name, cwd, no focus steal unless `--focus`). Its initial pane becomes agent pane #1.
3. **Split** to N (+1 if `--with-orch`) panes: repeatedly split the largest pane, alternating orientation — gives a rough grid whose exact ratios don't matter because…
4. **Balance** via the PR #1 `layout.balance` logic once the count is right.
5. **Label** each pane (existing rename path) and **join** each to msg group `<team-name>` — membership established *before* any agent starts, so no agent can send into a group its teammates haven't joined yet.
6. **Send command text** to each pane last (same `PaneSendInput` mechanism as `pane run`). ConPTY buffers typed input until the shell reads it, so shell-startup racing should be safe — but this is explicitly on the live-e2e verify list, not assumed.
7. Return the pane map; CLI prints it (`--json` or aligned table).

`--wait` (client-side): poll pane agent state until every roster pane reports something other than `unknown` (i.e., the detect module recognized a running agent). Entries whose command isn't a detectable agent (e.g. `pwsh` passthrough, and the orch pane always) are excluded and listed as `not detectable` in the wait report rather than blocking it.

## Section 5: Error handling

- **Parse-time (exit 2, nothing created):** empty roster; duplicate labels; label `orch` used in the roster together with `--with-orch`; labels/team name violating msg addressing syntax (no `@`, `/`, or whitespace — same charset the msg bus resolver already enforces).
- **Team-name collision:** if msg group `<name>` already has members, refuse (exit 1, "team already exists — pick another name or close the old workspace"). Prevents silently merging two teams' inboxes.
- **Server-side failure at any step:** close the just-created workspace — cascading pane + group teardown rides the msg-teardown path hardened in PR #2 — and return one error naming the failed step and pane. No half-built teams.
- **Exit codes:** 0 success; 2 usage; 1 spawn failed (rolled back); 3 `--wait` timeout — *spawn succeeded*, pane map is still printed, per-pane readiness states included. Orchestrators must be able to tell "team is up but an agent is slow" from "no team".

## Section 6: Testing

- **Unit:** roster parsing (labels, dupes, passthrough with quoting/spaces), registry resolution precedence, label/name validation.
- **Integration (test-server harness, like the msg-bus suite):** spawn with `pwsh`-style passthrough entries → assert workspace exists, N panes with expected labels, `msg who` shows full group membership, layout is balanced, each pane received its command text (via pane read); rollback test — force a mid-spawn failure and assert no workspace/group residue; name-collision refusal.
- **Protocol 19 bump:** all four checklist sites (`wire.rs`, schema regen, `api_ping.rs`, `cli_wrapper.rs`, `tests/support/mod.rs`).
- **Live e2e before PR (real binary, per house practice):** spawn a real mixed team (`claude` + `grok --always-approve`), confirm agents actually boot, `--wait` reaches ready, msg round-trips between two spawned panes, and the shell-startup input-buffering assumption from Section 4 holds.

That's the full design. Look right? If yes, I'll write the spec doc, self-review it, and hand it to you for final review before the implementation plan.

{"file_path": "K:\\Downloads\\__Projects.Mine\\herdr4Windows\\docs\\superpowers\\specs\\2026-07-18-team-spawn-design.md", "content": "# Team Spawn Primitive — Design Spec\n\nDate: 2026-07-18\nStatus: approved by Tony (brainstorm session)\nBuilds on: pane balance (PR #1, protocol 17), msg bus (PR #2, protocol 18)\n\n## Problem\n\nStanding up an agent team today means hand-scripting: `workspace create`, N × `pane split`, N × `pane rename`, N × `pane run`, N × `msg group join`, `pane balance`. It is slow, racy, and partial failures leave half-built workspaces. Orchestrators (Claude Code or scripts driving herdrplus via CLI) need one command that produces a ready-to-address team and returns the label→pane map.\n\n## Decisions\n\n- **Server-native** `team.spawn` wire method (protocol 19), matching the precedent of pane balance and msg bus. One request, one owner of rollback, reusable later by the TUI.\n- Mixed roster via `--agents`, labels auto-generated with optional `label=` override per entry.\n- Agent launch commands resolved server-side from a new `[team.agents]` config registry; unknown names pass through verbatim as commands.\n- Orchestrator pane is opt-in via `--with-orch [cmd]`.\n- Spawn returns immediately; `--wait` (client-side polling) is opt-in.\n- One shared `--cwd` for the whole team. Worktree-per-agent stays out of v1 (agent CLIs like grok's `--worktree` already cover it via registry config).\n\n## CLI surface\n\n```\nherdrplus team spawn <team-name>\n    --agents <entry>[,<entry>...]     # entry = agent | label=agent\n    [--cwd <dir>]                     # shared by all panes; default: caller's cwd\n    [--with-orch [cmd]]               # extra pane labeled \"orch\"; default cmd = plain shell\n    [--wait] [--timeout <secs>]       # poll until all agent panes ready\n    [--json]                          # machine-readable pane map (default when stdout is not a tty)\n```\n\n- `<team-name>` becomes both the workspace label and the msg group name.\n- Label defaults: per-agent counters — `claude-1`, `claude-2`, `grok-1`. Explicit labels via `ws1=claude`.\n- Example: `herdrplus team spawn review --agents ws1=claude,ws2=claude,reviewer=grok --wait`\n- Output pane map: `{workspace_id, group, panes: [{label, pane_id, agent, command}]}`.\n- Out of scope v1: `team status` (covered by `pane list` + `msg who`); teardown (covered by `workspace close`, whose msg-group cascade shipped in PR #2).\n\n## Agent registry (config)\n\nNew optional config section; values are full command lines typed into the pane's shell (same mechanism as `pane run` / `PaneSendInput` — no argv parsing by herdrplus):\n\n```toml\n[team.agents]\nclaude = \"claude --dangerously-skip-permissions\"\nagy    = \"agy --continue --dangerously-skip-permissions\"\ngrok   = \"grok --always-approve\"\nomp    = \"omp --approval-mode yolo\"\npi     = \"pi\"                          # pi has no approval prompts; runs YOLO by default\n```\n\n(Flags verified against the installed CLIs on 2026-07-18: grok also accepts `--permission-mode bypassPermissions`; omp also accepts `--auto-approve`.)\n\n- Resolution is **server-side** (server owns config).\n- Registry hit → configured command string. Miss → the roster entry name itself is the command, verbatim (quoted entries like `--agents \"ws1=pwsh -NoLogo\"` work).\n\n## Wire method\n\n- `team.spawn`, protocol bumped to **19** (strict-equality client/server gate).\n- Bump checklist (all four sites): `src/protocol/wire.rs`, schema artifact regen, `tests/api_ping.rs`, `tests/cli_wrapper.rs`, `tests/support/mod.rs`.\n- Params: `{name, entries: [{label?, agent}], cwd?, orch_command??, focus?}`.\n  (`orch_command` is present-with-default vs absent: absent = no orch pane; present-null/empty = plain shell.)\n- Result: the pane map above.\n\n## Data flow (server handler, in order)\n\n1. **Resolve** every roster entry against `[team.agents]`. Any failure aborts before creation.\n2. **Create workspace** (label = team name, cwd; no focus steal unless `focus`). Its initial pane is agent pane #1.\n3. **Split** to N (+1 for orch) panes: repeatedly split the largest pane, alternating orientation.\n4. **Balance** via the PR #1 `layout.balance` logic.\n5. **Label** each pane (existing rename path) and **join** each to msg group `<team-name>` — membership complete before any agent starts, so no early send hits a partially-joined group.\n6. **Send command text** to each pane last (`PaneSendInput` + Enter). ConPTY buffers typed input until the shell reads it, so shell-startup racing is expected-safe — explicitly on the live-e2e verify list, not assumed.\n7. Return the pane map.\n\n`--wait` (client-side): poll pane agent state until every roster pane reports a state other than `unknown` (detect module recognized a running agent), or timeout. Panes whose command is not a detectable agent (e.g. `pwsh` passthrough; the orch pane always) are excluded and reported as `not detectable`. Note: detect currently knows claude/codex/gemini/pi; omp may classify as pi or unknown — live e2e will tell.\n\n## Error handling\n\n- **Parse-time (exit 2, nothing created):** empty roster; duplicate labels; label `orch` in roster combined with `--with-orch`; labels/team name violating msg addressing syntax (no `@`, `/`, whitespace — same charset the msg resolver enforces).\n- **Team-name collision (exit 1):** if msg group `<name>` already has members, refuse: \"team already exists — pick another name or close the old workspace\". Prevents merging two teams' inboxes.\n- **Server-side failure at any step:** close the just-created workspace (cascading pane + msg-group teardown rides the PR #2-hardened path); return one error naming the failed step and pane. No half-built teams.\n- **Exit codes:** 0 success; 2 usage; 1 spawn failed (rolled back); 3 `--wait` timeout — spawn *succeeded*, pane map still printed with per-pane readiness. Orchestrators must distinguish \"team up, agent slow\" from \"no team\".\n\n## Testing\n\n- **Unit:** roster parsing (labels, dupes, passthrough with quotes/spaces), registry resolution precedence, label/name validation.\n- **Integration (test-server harness):** spawn with passthrough entries → workspace exists, N panes with expected labels, `msg who` shows full membership, layout balanced, each pane received its command text (`pane read`); forced mid-spawn failure → no workspace/group residue; name-collision refusal.\n- **Protocol 19:** all four checklist sites updated.\n- **Live e2e before PR (real binary):** spawn a real mixed team (`claude` + `grok`), agents boot, `--wait` reaches ready, msg round-trip between two spawned panes, and the ConPTY input-buffering assumption holds.\n\n## Review provenance\n\nBrainstormed and approved in-session 2026-07-18. External review (Sol56) expected at implementation-diff stage, per the two-reviewer gate.\n"}

# Writing Plans

## Overview

Write comprehensive implementation plans assuming the engineer has zero context for our codebase and questionable taste. Document everything they need to know: which files to touch for each task, code, testing, docs they might need to check, how to test it. Give them the whole plan as bite-sized tasks. DRY. YAGNI. TDD. Frequent commits.

Assume they are a skilled developer, but know almost nothing about our toolset or problem domain. Assume they don't know good test design very well.

**Announce at start:** "I'm using the writing-plans skill to create the implementation plan."

**Context:** If working in an isolated worktree, it should have been created via the `superpowers:using-git-worktrees` skill at execution time.

**Save plans to:** `docs/superpowers/plans/YYYY-MM-DD-<feature-name>.md`
- (User preferences for plan location override this default)

## Scope Check

If the spec covers multiple independent subsystems, it should have been broken into sub-project specs during brainstorming. If it wasn't, suggest breaking this into separate plans — one per subsystem. Each plan should produce working, testable software on its own.

## File Structure

Before defining tasks, map out which files will be created or modified and what each one is responsible for. This is where decomposition decisions get locked in.

- Design units with clear boundaries and well-defined interfaces. Each file should have one clear responsibility.
- You reason best about code you can hold in context at once, and your edits are more reliable when files are focused. Prefer smaller, focused files over large ones that do too much.
- Files that change together should live together. Split by responsibility, not by technical layer.
- In existing codebases, follow established patterns. If the codebase uses large files, don't unilaterally restructure - but if a file you're modifying has grown unwieldy, including a split in the plan is reasonable.

This structure informs the task decomposition. Each task should produce self-contained changes that make sense independently.

## Task Right-Sizing

A task is the smallest unit that carries its own test cycle and is worth a
fresh reviewer's gate. When drawing task boundaries: fold setup,
configuration, scaffolding, and documentation steps into the task whose
deliverable needs them; split only where a reviewer could meaningfully
reject one task while approving its neighbor. Each task ends with an
independently testable deliverable.

## Bite-Sized Task Granularity

**Each step is one action (2-5 minutes):**
- "Write the failing test" - step
- "Run it to make sure it fails" - step
- "Implement the minimal code to make the test pass" - step
- "Run the tests and make sure they pass" - step
- "Commit" - step

## Plan Document Header

**Every plan MUST start with this header:**

```markdown
# [Feature Name] Implementation Plan

> **For agentic workers:** REQUIRED SUB-SKILL: Use superpowers:subagent-driven-development (recommended) or superpowers:executing-plans to implement this plan task-by-task. Steps use checkbox (`- [ ]`) syntax for tracking.

**Goal:** [One sentence describing what this builds]

**Architecture:** [2-3 sentences about approach]

**Tech Stack:** [Key technologies/libraries]

## Global Constraints

[The spec's project-wide requirements — version floors, dependency limits,
naming and copy rules, platform requirements — one line each, with exact
values copied verbatim from the spec. Every task's requirements implicitly
include this section.]

---
```

## Task Structure

````markdown
### Task N: [Component Name]

**Files:**
- Create: `exact/path/to/file.py`
- Modify: `exact/path/to/existing.py:123-145`
- Test: `tests/exact/path/to/test.py`

**Interfaces:**
- Consumes: [what this task uses from earlier tasks — exact signatures]
- Produces: [what later tasks rely on — exact function names, parameter
  and return types. A task's implementer sees only their own task; this
  block is how they learn the names and types neighboring tasks use.]

- [ ] **Step 1: Write the failing test**

```python
def test_specific_behavior():
    result = function(input)
    assert result == expected
```

- [ ] **Step 2: Run test to verify it fails**

Run: `pytest tests/path/test.py::test_name -v`
Expected: FAIL with "function not defined"

- [ ] **Step 3: Write minimal implementation**

```python
def function(input):
    return expected
```

- [ ] **Step 4: Run test to verify it passes**

Run: `pytest tests/path/test.py::test_name -v`
Expected: PASS

- [ ] **Step 5: Commit**

```bash
git add tests/path/test.py src/path/file.py
git commit -m "feat: add specific feature"
```
````

## No Placeholders

Every step must contain the actual content an engineer needs. These are **plan failures** — never write them:
- "TBD", "TODO", "implement later", "fill in details"
- "Add appropriate error handling" / "add validation" / "handle edge cases"
- "Write tests for the above" (without actual test code)
- "Similar to Task N" (repeat the code — the engineer may be reading tasks out of order)
- Steps that describe what to do without showing how (code blocks required for code steps)
- References to types, functions, or methods not defined in any task

## Remember
- Exact file paths always
- Complete code in every step — if a step changes code, show the code
- Exact commands with expected output
- DRY, YAGNI, TDD, frequent commits

## Self-Review

After writing the complete plan, look at the spec with fresh eyes and check the plan against it. This is a checklist you run yourself — not a subagent dispatch.

**1. Spec coverage:** Skim each section/requirement in the spec. Can you point to a task that implements it? List any gaps.

**2. Placeholder scan:** Search your plan for red flags — any of the patterns from the "No Placeholders" section above. Fix them.

**3. Type consistency:** Do the types, method signatures, and property names you used in later tasks match what you defined in earlier tasks? A function called `clearLayers()` in Task 3 but `clearFullLayers()` in Task 7 is a bug.

If you find issues, fix them inline. No need to re-review — just fix and move on. If you find a spec requirement with no task, add the task.

## Execution Handoff

After saving the plan, offer execution choice:

**"Plan complete and saved to `docs/superpowers/plans/<filename>.md`. Two execution options:**

**1. Subagent-Driven (recommended)** - I dispatch a fresh subagent per task, review between tasks, fast iteration

**2. Inline Execution** - Execute tasks in this session using executing-plans, batch execution with checkpoints

**Which approach?"**

**If Subagent-Driven chosen:**
- **REQUIRED SUB-SKILL:** Use superpowers:subagent-driven-development
- Fresh subagent per task + two-stage review

**If Inline Execution chosen:**
- **REQUIRED SUB-SKILL:** Use superpowers:executing-plans
- Batch execution with checkpoints for review

<agent-message from="explore-cli-config">
CLI + Config surface map for `herdrplus team spawn` and `[team.agents]`. All paths under `__references/herdr/`.

## 1. Top-level CLI dispatch — adding a `team` namespace
`src/cli.rs:63` `pub fn maybe_run(args: &[String]) -> io::Result<CommandOutcome>` is the single dispatch point. Reads `args[1]`, matches namespace string in one `match` (`src/cli.rs:68-93`); each arm calls `<module>::run_<x>_command(&args[2..])` returning `i32`, wrapped in `CommandOutcome::Handled`. Unknown → `_ => Ok(CommandOutcome::NotCli)` (`:92`).
To add: `mod team;` in the module list (`:13-28`), and arm `"team" => team::run_team_command(&args[2..])?,` next to `"msg"` (`:87`).
NO clap/derive. NO central "list of namespaces" help — each namespace hand-rolls its own `print_<x>_help()` to stderr + returns exit 2 on bad input. `msg::run_msg_command` (`src/cli/msg.rs:25`) is the structural model to copy: match `args[0]` subcommand → `team_spawn(&args[1..])`, default arm prints help + returns 2.

## 2. Shared CLI helpers (in `src/cli.rs`, `pub(super)`, called as `super::`)
- `send_request(&Request) -> io::Result<serde_json::Value>` (`:997`) — protocol-checks then sends, returns raw JSON.
- `send_ok_request(method: Method) -> io::Result<i32>` (`:983`) — sends; on error prints JSON to stderr + returns 1; else returns 0 printing nothing.
- `print_response(&serde_json::Value) -> io::Result<i32>` (`:973`) — THE standard result printer: if `response.get("error").is_some()` → eprintln JSON, return 1; else println JSON, return 0.
- `normalize_pane_id(v)` (`:1057`) is currently IDENTITY (`v.to_string()`); canonicalization is server-side. Same for workspace/tab (`:1049`,`:1053`).
- `parse_env_assignment(raw) -> Result<(String,String),String>` (`:45`) — split first `=`, reject empty key + NUL, allows empty value.
- `parse_u32_flag`/`parse_u64_flag(flag, value)` (`:1118`,`:1124`).

OUTPUT CONVENTION: for API-backed commands it is **JSON always, never tables**. Every `msg` subcommand prints raw server JSON via `print_response` — e.g. `msg who` (`src/cli/msg.rs:650`) just forwards `ResponseResult::MsgWho`. The only table printer (`print_session_table`, `:1162`) is for LOCAL non-API data and is gated behind `--json` (`session list [--json]`, `:443`). So `team spawn` output = print server JSON via `print_response`; add `--json`/table only for CLI-computed data.

## 3. Connection + no-server behavior
Transport: `interprocess` local sockets — Unix domain socket on Unix, **named pipe on Windows** (`src/ipc.rs:29` `connect_local_stream`, `GenericNamespaced` on Windows `:38-45`). Wire = newline-delimited JSON (`src/api/client.rs:56-62`,`:207-223`). `ApiClient::local()` (`:39`) targets default session socket.
NO SERVER: `send_request` → `ensure_server_protocol_compatible` (`src/cli.rs:1011`) → `client.status()` Ping → `connect()` (`src/api/client.rs:128`) returns an `io::Error` (refused/pipe-not-found) that propagates via `api_client_error_to_io` (`:1042`) out of `maybe_run` as `Result::Err` → main prints + non-zero exit. No auto-start. Timeouts are best-effort: Windows named pipes return `ErrorKind::Unsupported` on `set_recv_timeout`, silently ignored (`src/api/client.rs:138-153`) — why `msg wait` does its own channel pacing.

## 4. Config end-to-end (definition → parse → server access)
DEFINITION: `Config` struct `src/config/model.rs:287-301`, `#[derive(Debug,Default,Deserialize)] #[serde(default)]`, flat sections: theme/terminal/session/update/keys/ui/worktrees/advanced/experimental/remote. Each section is its own `#[serde(default)]` struct + `Default` impl.
BEST MODEL TO COPY = `SessionConfig` (`:244-258`): one-field section, manual Default, wired in 3 spots. For a name→command map, use `BTreeMap<String,String>` (serde parses a TOML string-table natively, no custom deserializer):
```
#[derive(Debug, Default, Deserialize)] #[serde(default)]
pub struct TeamConfig { pub agents: std::collections::BTreeMap<String,String> }
```
then `pub team: TeamConfig,` in `Config` (`:287`), and re-export `TeamConfig` in the `pub use self::model::{...}` block (`src/config.rs:21-26`).

TWO PARSE PATHS, BOTH MUST BE UPDATED:
1. Startup: `Config::load()` (`src/config/io.rs:104`) does one `toml::from_str::<Config>` (`:125`). Auto-parses a new `#[serde(default)]` section.
2. Live reload: `load_live_config_from_str` (`:223`) parses SECTION-BY-SECTION via explicit `load_live_section(table,"session",...)` calls (`:247-326`). MUST add `load_live_section(table,"team","team config",...,|s| config.team = s)` or `[team]` is dropped on reload.
3. Unknown-section guard: `KNOWN_TOP_LEVEL_CONFIG_KEYS` (`:7-19`) is a hardcoded allowlist — MUST add `"team"` or every reload emits `unknown config section [team]; ignoring section`.

SERVER-SIDE ACCESS (key fact): the server does NOT keep a `Config` on state. Config values are FLATTENED into individual `AppState` fields. At construction `App::new(config: &Config, ...)` (`src/app/mod.rs:355`) reads e.g. `config.terminal.default_shell`, `config.advanced.scrollback_limit_bytes` into state (`:400-404`,`:473-474`). On reload `apply_config_from_disk` (`:1313`) → `load_live_config()` → `apply_live_config` (`:1341`) copies each section into `self.state.*`, gated by `invalid_section("terminal")` etc. (`:1489-1493`), returning `ConfigReloadReport { status: Applied|Partial|Failed, diagnostics }` (`src/config/model.rs:262-272`).
For `team spawn` the handler needs the agents map. Two options: (a) mirror the pattern — add `self.state.team_agents: BTreeMap` populated in `App::new` + `apply_live_config` (matches every section, picks up live reloads free); (b) re-read `crate::config::Config::load().config.team.agents` at request time (exactly what `run_channel_command` does, `src/cli.rs:102`) — simpler but misses unsaved reloads + re-reads file per call. Recommend (a).
API dispatch: `src/app/api.rs:875` `match request.method`, msg arms at `:1122-1127`. Add `Method::TeamSpawn(params) => return self.handle_team_spawn(...)`, handler in new `src/app/api/team.rs` modeled on `src/app/api/msg.rs`. Schema (params/Method variant/ResponseResult variant) lives in `src/api/schema/` (msg example `src/api/schema/msg.rs`).

## 5. Label / group-name charset validation (server-side, `src/msg.rs`)
- `MsgBus::parse_target(expr)` (`:146`): empty → Unaddressable; `@x` → Group (`@all` special → All), but `@`+`/` or bare `@` → Unaddressable (`:151-159`); canonical `w<ENC>:p<ENC>` grammar → PaneId (`is_public_pane_id`, `:456`); `ws/label` where label must be nonempty, no `/`, not start `@` → Qualified (`:165-177`); else bare Label. A lone `:` does NOT make a pane id — `worker:api` is a legal label. NO whitespace/most-punctuation restriction — only `/`, leading `@`, emptiness rejected.
- `validate_group_name(group)` (`:472-478`): reject if `is_empty() || contains('/') || starts_with('@')`. Same 3 rules. Called from `group_join`/`group_leave` (`:348`,`:363`).
There is NO stricter shared identifier validator to reuse. If team agent names must be addressable as labels, enforce the same 3 constraints yourself.

## 6. Exit codes + server-error printing
0 = success. 2 = usage/bad args (always paired with eprintln usage string). 1 = runtime failure incl. any server-returned error.
Server errors are wire objects `{"error":{"code":"...","message":"..."}}` built by `encode_error(id,code,message)` (`src/app/api/msg.rs:23`; codes enumerated in `resolve_error_response` `:303-343`: pane_not_found, unknown_target, ambiguous_target, empty_group, unaddressable_label, message_too_large, invalid_group_name). CLI detects uniformly via `response.get("error").is_some()`, prints whole JSON to stderr, returns 1 (`print_response` `src/cli.rs:973-980`; `send_ok_request` `:989-994`). CLI does NOT translate codes to prose — forwards JSON.

# `team.spawn` wire-method plumbing — end-to-end trace

All paths under `K:\Downloads\__Projects.Mine\herdr4Windows\__references\herdr\`. A composed `team.spawn` touches the same 6 sites every method does; the headless socket path needs NO changes (it forwards to the same App dispatch).

## 1. Method enum + Params/Result registration
**Method enum — single site:** `src\api\schema.rs:47-244` (`enum Method`, `#[serde(tag="method", content="params")]`). Variants are `#[serde(rename="wire.name")] Variant(ParamsStruct)`:
- `:68` `#[serde(rename="workspace.create")] WorkspaceCreate(WorkspaceCreateParams)`
- `:140` `#[serde(rename="layout.balance")] LayoutBalance(LayoutBalanceParams)` — **pane balance is `layout.balance`, NOT `pane.balance`**
- `:238` `#[serde(rename="msg.group_join")] MsgGroupJoin(MsgGroupJoinParams)` — wire name is `msg.group_join` (underscore)

`Request` wrapper: `src\api\schema.rs:35-40` = `{ id: String, #[serde(flatten)] method: Method }`. Wire shape `{"id":"..","method":"workspace.create","params":{..}}`.

**Params/Result structs** in per-domain modules under `src\api\schema\`, re-exported `pub use <mod>::*` at `schema.rs:17-29`. All derive `Debug,Clone,PartialEq,[Eq,]Serialize,Deserialize,schemars::JsonSchema`. Verbatim:
- `WorkspaceCreateParams` `schema\workspaces.rs:7-17`: `cwd:Option<String>`, `focus:bool`(#[serde(default)]), `label:Option<String>`, `env:HashMap<String,String>`
- `LayoutBalanceParams` `schema\panes.rs:144-150`: `tab_id:Option<String>`, `pane_id:Option<String>` (mutually exclusive)
- `MsgGroupJoinParams` `schema\msg.rs:59-62`: `pane_id:String`, `group:String`
- `PaneSplitParams` `schema\panes.rs:11-26`: `workspace_id:Option<String>`, `target_pane_id:Option<String>`, `direction:SplitDirection`, `ratio:Option<f32>`, `cwd:Option<String>`, `focus:bool`, `env:HashMap`
- `PaneRenameParams` `schema\panes.rs:231-236`: `pane_id:String`, `label:Option<String>`
- `PaneSendInputParams` `schema\panes.rs:250-257`: `pane_id:String`, `text:String`, `keys:Vec<String>`

## 2. Server routing + dispatch + handler state
**Two entry points, one shared dispatch.**
1. In-app: `App::handle_api_request` `src\app\api.rs:861` → `handle_api_request_after_internal_events_drained` `:866`, holding the giant `match request.method` at `:875-1135`. Arms: `WorkspaceCreate` `:951`, `LayoutBalance` `:1015`, `MsgGroupJoin` `:1125`; fallthrough `_ => encode_error(.., "not_implemented", ..)` `:1128`.
2. Headless socket: `HeadlessServer::handle_api_request_with_shutdown_check_inner` `src\server\headless.rs:2985`. Special-cases a few (live-handoff, notifications, client-title, worktree.create/remove deferred `:3111-3119`, reload-config) then **falls through to `self.app.handle_api_request_after_internal_events_drained(msg.request)` at `:3143-3144`**. So `team.spawn` needs only a handler in path (1). Requests arrive as `api::ApiRequestMessage{request,respond_to,response_write_complete}` (`src\api\mod.rs:78-82`) over `ApiRequestSender` mpsc (`:84`); accept loop `api::start_server(..)` called `headless.rs:1287`.

**Handler signature:** `impl App` methods `pub(super) fn handle_x(&mut self, id: String, params: XParams) -> String` returning encoded JSON. State via `self.state` (`workspaces:Vec<Workspace>`, `terminals`, `msg_bus`, `active:Option<usize>`) and `self.terminal_runtimes`. Modules declared `app\api.rs:4-16`.

**msg.group_join handler:** `App::handle_msg_group_join` `src\app\api\msg.rs:217-232`. Canonicalizes pane id via `self.canonical_pane_id` (`:13-16` = `parse_pane_id`+`public_pane_id` — bus is keyed ONLY on canonical public ids), then **`self.state.msg_bus.group_join(&pane_id, &params.group)`** → `Ok(Vec<String>)`/`Err(MsgError)`. Bus method `MsgBus::group_join` `src\msg.rs:347-358` (validates name, inserts into `group_members`+`pane_groups`, idempotent). Success → `ResponseResult::MsgGroup{groups}`.

## 3. workspace.create + workspace.close
**Create:** `App::handle_workspace_create` `src\app\api\workspaces.rs:38-71`. Resolves cwd (default focused-pane cwd `:43-49`), normalizes env `super::env::normalize_launch_env(params.env)` `:50-53`, calls **`self.create_workspace_with_launch_env(cwd, focus, extra_env)` → Ok(index:usize)** (`src\app\creation.rs:192-226`) which **creates the workspace AND its root pane** (root = `workspaces[idx].tabs[0].root_pane`). Applies label `workspace.set_custom_name` `:56-60`, emits open events `emit_workspace_open_events` (`creation.rs:296-312` → WorkspaceCreated+TabCreated+PaneCreated+LayoutUpdated), returns `workspace_created_result(index)` (`creation.rs:340-349`) → **`ResponseResult::WorkspaceCreated{workspace:WorkspaceInfo, tab:TabInfo, root_pane:PaneInfo}`** (`schema\response.rs:57-61`). Caller reads new workspace_id + root pane_id from the response.

**Close (teardown cascade):** `App::handle_workspace_close` `workspaces.rs:227-251`. Sets `state.selected=index`, then **`self.state.close_selected_workspace()`** (`src\app\actions.rs:1524`) — owns FULL teardown incl. plugin-pane records **and msg-bus purge** for every workspace in the close set (linked-worktree group members too). Then `shutdown_detached_terminal_runtimes()`, emits WorkspaceClosed. (Msg-bus teardown lives inside `close_selected_workspace`, per comment `workspaces.rs:237-240`.)

## 4. pane.split + pane.rename
**Split:** `App::handle_pane_split` `src\app\api\panes.rs:32-124`. Resolves target: explicit `target_pane_id` → else `workspace_id` focused → else active focused (`:33-45`) → `(ws_idx, target_pane_id)`. Normalizes env, `estimate_pane_size()`, follow-cwd. Calls **`ws.split_pane_with_ratio(..)` / `ws.split_pane(..)`** (`:70-96`) → `Some(Ok((target_tab_idx, new_pane:NewPane)))`. direction: `Right→Horizontal`, `Down→Vertical` (`:65-68`). Inserts runtime/terminal, `pane_info(ws_idx, new_pane.pane_id)`, emits PaneCreated+LayoutUpdated. Returns **`ResponseResult::PaneInfo{pane}`** — new id = `pane.pane_id`.

**Rename/label:** `App::handle_pane_rename` `panes.rs:1149-1173`. Pane → `terminal_id` → `terminal.set_manual_label(label)` (non-empty trimmed) else `terminal.clear_manual_label()` (`:1165-1168`). **manual_label is exactly what the msg bus uses for label addressing** (read in `app\api\msg.rs:46,105,260`). Returns `PaneInfo{pane}`. (Layout-apply has a parallel `apply_layout_pane_label` `app\api\layouts.rs:498-519`.)

## 5. layout.balance internal + pane.send_input
**Balance:** `App::handle_layout_balance` `src\app\api\layouts.rs:257-287`. Resolves `(ws_idx,tab_idx)` via `resolve_layout_export_target` (`:289-308` — tab_id XOR pane_id; both→None→`layout_not_found`; neither→active ws active tab), then **`tab.layout.balance()`** — **per-tab, on the Node tree, returns bool changed**. Returns **`ResponseResult::LayoutBalanced{layout:LayoutDescription, changed:bool}`**; emits LayoutUpdated only when changed (`:282-285`). Balance is per-tab (tab_id/pane_id), NOT per-workspace.

**Send text+Enter:** `App::handle_pane_send_input` `panes.rs:1501-1529`. Pane → `lookup_runtime_sender`. `encode_api_keys(runtime,&params.keys)`; if text non-empty `encode_api_text(runtime,&params.text)`; writes via `runtime.try_send_bytes(Bytes::from(..))`. **For "text then Enter" pass `text:"..", keys:vec!["enter"]`** — text bytes first (`:1516-1521`) then each key (`:1522-1526`). Returns `Ok{}`. (`pane.send_text` `:1483` text-only; `pane.send_keys` `:1604` keys-only.)

## 6. Result/error shaping
`encode_success(id, ResponseResult::Variant{..})` / `encode_error(id, "code", "message")` — both `src\app\api\responses.rs`, imported per-handler `use super::responses::{encode_error, encode_success}`. `ResponseResult` tagged enum `schema\response.rs:42-44` (`#[serde(tag="type", rename_all="snake_case")]`); new method needs its own variant here (e.g. `TeamSpawned{workspace, panes:Vec<PaneInfo>}`).
**msg error codes (protocol 18)** mapped `app\api\msg.rs:303-343` (`resolve_error_response`): `pane_not_found`, `unknown_target`, `ambiguous_target`, `empty_group`, `unaddressable_label`; plus `message_too_large`/`invalid_group_name` from `MsgError` (`src\msg.rs:51-54`), `MAX_MESSAGE_BODY_BYTES`=64KiB (`msg.rs:14`). Common codes: `workspace_not_found`, `pane_not_found`, `pane_split_failed`, `workspace_create_failed`, `layout_not_found`, `invalid_key`, `pane_send_failed`. Error wire shape `ErrorResponse{id, error:ErrorBody{code,message}}`.

## 7. Schema artifact + PROTOCOL_VERSION
- **Generated file:** `docs\next\api\herdr-api.schema.json`, bundled via `include_str!(..)` at `src\cli\api.rs:1` (served by `herdr api schema`).
- **Regen:** fully schemars-reflected over `Request` — `protocol_schema_document()` `src\api\schema\tests.rs:32-46` calls `schemars::schema_for!(Request)` (recurses Method + all Params). Guard test `generated_protocol_schema_artifact_is_current` `tests.rs:91-117` fails when stale; regenerate with **`HERDR_UPDATE_API_SCHEMA=1`** (`:100-103`). No build.rs. On this repo the test bin is `herdrplus` (`cargo test --bin herdrplus`). So: add Method variant + Params/Result (they carry JsonSchema) → run that test once with the env var.
- **PROTOCOL_VERSION:** `src\protocol\wire.rs:16` = `pub const PROTOCOL_VERSION: u32 = 18;`. Bumping touches only that const; read at `api\server.rs:318`, `cli\status.rs`, `cli\protocol_guard.rs:21` (exact-match client/server gate), `app\api\session.rs:47`, schema header (`tests.rs:37`). An additive method doesn't strictly REQUIRE a bump, but project convention bumps per wire-surface add, and protocol_guard rejects mismatches — bump if you want old clients rejected.
- **Do-not-miss extra site:** `request_changes_ui` `src\api\mod.rs:22-76` lists every method that dirties the UI so headless re-renders. WorkspaceCreate/LayoutBalance/PaneSplit/PaneRename/MsgSend all listed (`:28,44,48,55,73`). **Add `Method::TeamSpawn(_)` here** or the grid won't repaint until the next event.

## 8. PaneAgentState API exposure
- Enum `PaneAgentState` `schema\common.rs:133-140`: snake_case **`Idle, Working, Blocked, Unknown`** (NO `Done`). It's the INPUT to `pane.report_agent` (`PaneReportAgentParams.state` `schema\panes.rs:328`).
- `PaneInfo` (`schema\panes.rs:402-436`) exposes **`agent_status: AgentStatus`** (`:425`) — the derived status — NOT `PaneAgentState`. `AgentStatus` (`common.rs:142-150`) has `Idle,Working,Blocked,Done,Unknown`. Other fields: `agent:Option<String>` `:416`, `display_agent` `:424`, `state_labels:HashMap` `:427`, `title` `:418`, `agent_session` `:432`. Conversion `PaneAgentState → AgentStatus` via `pane_agent_status(..)` (`app\api.rs:571-578`). **To monitor a spawned team, poll `pane.list`/`pane.get` and read `agent_status`.**

## Bottom line
`team.spawn` composes with zero new state primitives. Add: (1) `Method::TeamSpawn` variant `schema.rs`, (2) `TeamSpawnParams`/`TeamSpawnResult` (new `schema\team.rs` or reuse), (3) dispatch arm `app\api.rs:875` match, (4) `handle_team_spawn` calling `create_workspace_with_launch_env` → `ws.split_pane*` loop → `terminal.set_manual_label` → `msg_bus.group_join` → `tab.layout.balance()` → `runtime.try_send_bytes`, (5) `ResponseResult::TeamSpawned` `response.rs`, (6) register in `request_changes_ui` `api\mod.rs`, then `HERDR_UPDATE_API_SCHEMA=1` to refresh the schema json. Headless socket path unchanged.

1525	            }
1526	        }
1527

227	    pub(super) fn handle_workspace_close(&mut self, id: String, target: WorkspaceTarget) -> String {
228	        let Some(index) = self.parse_workspace_id(&target.workspace_id) else {
229	            return workspace_not_found(id, &target.workspace_id);
230	        };
231	        if self.state.workspaces.get(index).is_none() {
232	            return workspace_not_found(id, &target.workspace_id);
233	        }
234	        let workspace_id = self.public_workspace_id(index);
235	        let workspace = self.workspace_info(index);
236	        self.state.selected = index;
237	        // close_selected_workspace owns full teardown — plugin pane records
238	        // and msg-bus purge — for EVERY workspace in the close set, including
239	        // linked worktree group members closed alongside the requested one.
240	        self.state.close_selected_workspace();
241	        self.shutdown_detached_terminal_runtimes();
242	        self.emit_event(EventEnvelope {
243	            event: EventKind::WorkspaceClosed,
244	            data: EventData::WorkspaceClosed {
245	                workspace_id,
246	                workspace: Some(workspace),
247	            },
248	        });
249	
250	        encode_success(id, ResponseResult::Ok {})
251	    }

not_implemented / missing functions)\n\n- [ ] **Step 3: Implement the handler**\n\n`src/app/api/team.rs` (complete implementation; adjust only where noted):\n\n```rust\nuse crate::api::schema::{\n    LayoutBalanceParams, MsgGroupJoinParams, PaneRenameParams, PaneSendInputParams,\n    PaneSplitParams, ResponseResult, SplitDirection, SuccessResponse, TeamPaneInfo,\n    TeamSpawnParams, WorkspaceCreateParams, WorkspaceTarget,\n};\nuse crate::app::App;\nuse crate::app::api::responses::{encode_error, encode_success};\nuse std::collections::HashMap;\n\n/// Test-only fault injection points for exercising rollback.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq)]\npub(super) enum TeamSpawnFault {\n    AfterSplits,\n}\n\nfn valid_name(s: &str) -> bool {\n    !s.is_empty()\n        && !s.contains('/')\n        && !s.starts_with('@')\n        && !s.chars().any(char::is_whitespace)\n}\n\n/// Parse a sibling handler's JSON reply; Ok(result) on success, Err(code: message) on error.\nfn parse_reply(response: &str) -> Result<ResponseResult, String> {\n    if let Ok(success) = serde_json::from_str::<SuccessResponse>(response) {\n        return Ok(success.result);\n    }\n    let value: serde_json::Value = serde_json::from_str(response).unwrap_or_default();\n    let code = value[\"error\"][\"code\"].as_str().unwrap_or(\"unknown\");\n    let message = value[\"error\"][\"message\"].as_str().unwrap_or(\"unknown error\");\n    Err(format!(\"{code}: {message}\"))\n}\n\nfn pane_id_of(result: ResponseResult) -> Result<String, String> {\n    match result {\n        ResponseResult::PaneInfo { pane } => Ok(pane.pane_id),\n        other => Err(format!(\"unexpected reply: {other:?}\")),\n    }\n}\n\nimpl App {\n    pub(super) fn handle_team_spawn(&mut self, id: String, params: TeamSpawnParams) -> String {\n        self.handle_team_spawn_with_fault(id, params, None)\n    }\n\n    pub(super) fn handle_team_spawn_with_fault(\n        &mut self,\n        id: String,\n        params: TeamSpawnParams,\n        fault: Option<TeamSpawnFault>,\n    ) -> String {\n        // ---- validate everything before creating anything ----\n        if params.entries.is_empty() {\n            return encode_error(id, \"empty_roster\", \"at least one --agents entry is required\");\n        }\n        if !valid_name(&params.name) {\n            return encode_error(\n                id,\n                \"invalid_team_name\",\n                \"team name must be non-empty with no '/', leading '@', or whitespace\",\n            );\n        }\n        let mut labels: Vec<String> = Vec::with_capacity(params.entries.len());\n        let mut counters: HashMap<String, usize> = HashMap::new();\n        for entry in &params.entries {\n            let label = match &entry.label {\n                Some(label) => label.clone(),\n                None => {\n                    let n = counters.entry(entry.agent.clone()).or_insert(0);\n                    *n += 1;\n                    format!(\"{}-{}\", entry.agent, n)\n                }\n            };\n            if !valid_name(&label) || (params.with_orch && label == \"orch\") {\n                return encode_error(\n                    id,\n                    \"invalid_label\",\n                    format!(\"invalid pane label {label:?}\"),\n                );\n            }\n            if labels.contains(&label) {\n                return encode_error(id, \"duplicate_label\", format!(\"duplicate label {label:?}\"));\n            }\n            labels.push(label);\n        }\n        if !self.state.msg_bus.group_members(&params.name).is_empty() {\n            return encode_error(\n                id,\n                \"team_exists\",\n                format!(\n                    \"msg group {:?} already has members — pick another name or close the old workspace\",\n                    params.name\n                ),\n            );\n        }\n        let commands: Vec<String> = params\n            .entries\n            .iter()\n            .map(|e| {\n                self.state\n                    .team_agents\n                    .get(&e.agent)\n                    .cloned()\n                    .unwrap_or_else(|| e.agent.clone())\n            })\n            .collect();\n\n        // ---- create workspace (root pane = first team pane) ----\n        let created = self.handle_workspace_create(\n            format!(\"{id}:ws\"),\n            WorkspaceCreateParams {\n                cwd: params.cwd.clone(),\n                focus: params.focus,\n                label: Some(params.name.clone()),\n                env: HashMap::new(),\n            },\n        );\n        let (workspace, root_pane_id) = match parse_reply(&created) {\n            Ok(ResponseResult::WorkspaceCreated { workspace, root_pane, .. }) => {\n                (workspace, root_pane.pane_id)\n            }\n            Ok(other) => {\n                return encode_error(id, \"team_spawn_failed\", format!(\"workspace create: unexpected reply {other:?}\"))\n            }\n            Err(err) => return encode_error(id, \"team_spawn_failed\", format!(\"workspace create: {err}\")),\n        };\n        let workspace_id = workspace.workspace_id.clone();\n\n        // Everything after this point must roll back on failure.\n        macro_rules! fail {\n            ($step:expr, $err:expr) => {{\n                let _ = self.handle_workspace_close(\n                    format!(\"{id}:rollback\"),\n                    WorkspaceTarget { workspace_id: workspace_id.clone() },\n                );\n                return encode_error(\n                    id,\n                    \"team_spawn_failed\",\n                    format!(\"{} failed: {} (workspace rolled back)\", $step, $err),\n                );\n            }};\n        }\n\n        // ---- split to a rough row-major grid; balance() equalizes areas after ----\n        let total = params.entries.len() + usize::from(params.with_orch);\n        let cols = (total as f64).sqrt().ceil() as usize;\n        let mut pane_ids: Vec<String> = vec![root_pane_id.clone()];\n        let mut row_seeds: Vec<String> = vec![root_pane_id.clone()];\n        let rows = total.div_ceil(cols);\n        for _ in 1..rows {\n            let seed = row_seeds.last().cloned().unwrap();\n            match self.split_team_pane(&id, &seed, SplitDirection::Down, params.cwd.as_deref()) {\n                Ok(new_id) => {\n                    row_seeds.push(new_id.clone());\n                    pane_ids.push(new_id);\n                }\n                Err(err) => fail!(\"pane split\", err),\n            }\n        }\n        // fill each row left-to-right (row-major: row r holds entries r*cols..)\n        let mut grid: Vec<String> = Vec::with_capacity(total);\n        for (row, seed) in row_seeds.iter().enumerate() {\n            let count = (total - row * cols).min(cols);\n            let mut row_panes = vec![seed.clone()];\n            for _ in 1..count {\n                let target = row_panes.last().cloned().unwrap();\n                match self.split_team_pane(&id, &target, SplitDirection::Right, params.cwd.as_deref()) {\n                    Ok(new_id) => {\n                        pane_ids.push(new_id.clone());\n                        row_panes.push(new_id);\n                    }\n                    Err(err) => fail!(\"pane split\", err),\n                }\n            }\n            grid.extend(row_panes);\n        }\n        if fault == Some(TeamSpawnFault::AfterSplits) {\n            fail!(\"fault injection\", \"test-forced failure\");\n        }\n\n        // ---- balance the tab ----\n        let balanced = self.handle_layout_balance(\n            format!(\"{id}:balance\"),\n            LayoutBalanceParams { tab_id: None, pane_id: Some(root_pane_id.clone()) },\n        );\n        if let Err(err) = parse_reply(&balanced) {\n            fail!(\"layout balance\", err);\n        }\n\n        // ---- label + group-join every pane (before any agent launches) ----\n        let mut all_labels = labels.clone();\n        if params.with_orch {\n            all_labels.push(\"orch\".to_string());\n        }\n        for (pane_id, label) in grid.iter().zip(all_labels.iter()) {\n            let renamed = self.handle_pane_rename(\n                format!(\"{id}:rename\"),\n                PaneRenameParams { pane_id: pane_id.clone(), label: Some(label.clone()) },\n            );\n            if let Err(err) = parse_reply(&renamed) {\n                fail!(\"pane rename\", err);\n            }\n            let joined = self.handle_msg_group_join(\n                format!(\"{id}:join\"),\n                MsgGroupJoinParams { pane_id: pane_id.clone(), group: params.name.clone() },\n            );\n            if let Err(err) = parse_reply(&joined) {\n                fail!(\"group join\", err);\n            }\n        }\n\n        // ---- send launch commands last ----\n        let mut result_panes: Vec<TeamPaneInfo> = Vec::with_capacity(total);\n        for (i, (pane_id, label)) in grid.iter().zip(all_labels.iter()).enumerate() {\n            let (agent, command) = if i < params.entries.len() {\n                (params.entries[i].agent.clone(), commands[i].clone())\n            } else {\n                (\"orch\".to_string(), params.orch_command.clone().unwrap_or_default())\n            };\n            if !command.is_empty() {\n                let sent = self.handle_pane_send_input(\n                    format!(\"{id}:run\"),\n                    PaneSendInputParams {\n                        pane_id: pane_id.clone(),\n                        text: command.clone(),\n                        keys: vec![\"Enter\".into()],\n                    },\n                );\n                if let Err(err) = parse_reply(&sent) {\n                    fail!(\"command launch\", err);\n                }\n            }\n            result_panes.push(TeamPaneInfo {\n                label: label.clone(),\n                pane_id: pane_id.clone(),\n                agent,\n                command,\n            });\n        }\n\n        encode_success(\n            id,\n            ResponseResult::TeamSpawned { workspace, group: params.name, panes: result_panes },\n        )\n    }\n\n    fn split_team_pane(\n        &mut self,\n        id: &str,\n        target_pane_id: &str,\n        direction: SplitDirection,\n        cwd: Option<&str>,\n    ) -> Result<String, String> {\n        let response = self.handle_pane_split(\n            format!(\"{id}:split\"),\n            PaneSplitParams {\n                workspace_id: None,\n                target_pane_id: Some(target_pane_id.to_string()),\n                direction,\n                ratio: None,\n                cwd: cwd.map(str::to_string),\n                focus: false,\n                env: HashMap::new(),\n            },\n        );\n        parse_reply(&response).and_then(pane_id_of)\n    }\n}\n```\n\nImplementation notes:\n- `WorkspaceTarget` — confirm its exact field name    }\n        _ => {\n            print_team_help();\n            Ok(2)\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nfn print_team_help() {\n    eprintln!(\"usage: herdr team spawn <name> --agents <entry>[,<entry>...] [--cwd DIR] [--with-orch [CMD]] [--wait] [--timeout SECS]\");\n    eprintln!(\"  entry = <agent> | <label>=<agent>   (agent resolved via [team.agents] config; unknown names run verbatim)\");\n}\n\npub(super) fn parse_spawn_args(args: &[String]) -> Result<SpawnArgs, String> {\n    let mut name: Option<String> = None;\n    let mut entries: Vec<TeamSpawnEntry> = Vec::new();\n };\n    let wait = parsed.wait;\n    let timeout_secs = parsed.timeout_secs;\n    // Send via the same request/response plumbing msg uses:\n    // build a Request with read result.pane.agent_status.\n            let response = super::send_request(/* Request with the pane-get Method for pane_id */)?;\n            let status = response[\"result\"][\"pane\"][\"agent_status\"].as_str().unwrap_or(\"unknown\");\n            if status != \"unknown\" {\n                ready.push(pane_id);\n            }\n        }\n        for pane_id in ready {\n            if let Some(label) = pending.remove(&pane_id) {\n                eprintln!(\"ready: {label}\");\n            }\n        }\n        if !pending.is_empty() {\n            std::thread::sleep(std::time::Duration::from_millis(1000));\n        }\n    }\n    Ok(0)\n}\n```\n\nThe two `/* ... */` call sites are the only intentionally-incomplete spots: they must copy the exact `Request { id, method }` construction used by `src/cli/msg.rs` subcommands and `src/cli/pane.rs` `pane get` respectively — copy those few lines verbatim from the neighbors rather than inventing them.\n\nIn `src/cli.rs`: add `mod team;` to the module list and the dispatch arm `\"team\" => team::run_team_command(&args[2..])?,` next to `\"msg\"` (:87).
