[Tool Result (toolu_01N44fY5zTL84w31CA9jGKKn)]
1	# Changelog
2	
3	All notable changes to HerdrPlus will be documented in this file.
4	
5	The format is based on [Keep a Changelog](https://keepachangelog.com/en/1.1.0/),
6	and this project adheres to [Semantic Versioning](https://semver.org/spec/v2.0.0.html).
7	
8	This file is append-only: new entries go on top, existing entries are never rewritten.
9	
10	## [0.3.2] - 2026-07-18
11	
12	### Fixed
13	
14	- Closing a worktree group (parent + linked worktree workspaces) now purges msg-bus state for panes in EVERY closed workspace, not just the requested one — `close_selected_workspace` owns the teardown for all close paths (TUI, API `workspace.close`, worktree removal, last-pane cascade).
15	- Cross-workspace `pane.move` re-keys msg-bus state to the pane's new canonical public id: the inbox travels intact (seq/ack/dropped counters preserved) and group membership follows; nothing is stranded under the old id.
16	- `msg wait` no longer misses messages when a large `@all`/group broadcast evicts this pane's `MsgReceived` event from the 512-entry event ring: the subscription is now only a wake hint — the CLI re-lists the inbox on every wake or 250ms poll tick, with `--timeout` still bounding total wait.
17	- `msg read --after SEQ` no longer over-acks: it is peek-like (never auto-acks), since acking the highest displayed seq would silently mark skipped unread messages as read. Plain `msg read` still auto-acks the highest displayed seq.
18	- `msg.send` with a PROVIDED sender pane id that does not resolve to a live pane (blank, malformed, closed) now returns `pane_not_found` instead of storing the bogus id verbatim; only an absent sender id means external identity.
19	- Msg targets containing `:` are only treated as pane ids when they match the canonical public-pane-id grammar (`w<ENC>:p<ENC>`); labels like `worker:api` now route as labels.
20	- `msg.send` validates the 64 KiB body cap before resolution, so an empty fan-out (e.g. `@all` excluding the only pane) can no longer "accept" an oversized body; zero-recipient sends return an empty `delivered_to` with a `null` `message` instead of a bogus `seq: 0` message object (schema: `msg_send.message` is now nullable).
21	
22	## [0.3.1] - 2026-07-18
23	
24	### Fixed
25	
26	- Msg-bus state (inbox + group membership) is now torn down on every pane-removal path — process death (`handle_pane_died`), tab close, workspace close, and layout-apply tab replacement/rollback — not just API `pane.close`. Dead panes no longer leak inboxes or linger as `@group` members.
27	- `msg wait` missed-wakeup race: the CLI now subscribes to `MsgReceived` before taking the baseline `msg.list`; if unread messages already exist at baseline they are printed immediately without blocking.
28	- All `msg.*` handlers (`list`, `ack`, `group join/leave`, `send` sender) canonicalize the pane id via the public-id path, so alias forms (`p_N`, post-restore aliases) address the same inbox and group membership as the canonical id; stored `from_pane_id` and `@all` sender exclusion also use the canonical id.
29	- `msg.send` failures now return distinct wire error codes per the protocol-18 spec — `pane_not_found`, `unknown_target`, `ambiguous_target` (candidates formatted as `workspace_id/label (pane_id)`), `empty_group`, `unaddressable_label` — instead of a collapsed `invalid_target`.
30

Optional `--with-orch [cmd]` orchestrator pane, `--cwd` (defaults to caller's cwd), `--wait [--timeout secs]` readiness polling (ready = agent recognized OR agent state detected; exit 3 on timeout with team still up). Server-native wire method `team.spawn` composed from the existing workspace/pane/msg/layout handlers; rollback on partial failure closes the workspace through the hardened msg-teardown cascade and restores the caller's focus. Validation: reserved team name `all`, pane-id-shaped labels rejected, labels trimmed, duplicate labels refused, existing group names refused (`team_exists`), 24-pane cap (`team_too_large`).\n- `[team.agents]` config section: agent name → launch command registry (e.g. `claude = \"claude --dangerously-skip-permissions\"`); unknown roster names pass through verbatim as commands. Live-reloadable.\n- Roster grammar: `label=agent` only when the label is a simple identifier (`[A-Za-z0-9_-]+`); anything else is treated as a verbatim command, so `claude --model=x` launches as a command rather than misparsing as a label.\n\n### Changed\n\n- Protocol version 18 → 19 (strict-equality gate; schema artifact regenerated).\n\n### Provenance\n\n- Design + implementation reviewed externally (GPT-5.6 Sol, high effort): 5 major spec findings folded in pre-merge (readiness signal, reserved/shadowed names, cwd ownership, rollback focus restoration + documented atomicity contract, passthrough grammar).\n\n## [0.3.2] - 2026-07-18"}

854	        let (respond_to, response_rx) = response_channel();
855	        assert!(app.handle_deferred_worktree_api_request(request, respond_to));
856	        if let Ok(response) = response_rx.recv_timeout(std::time::Duration::from_millis(50)) {

864	            .expect("deferred API request should respond after completion event")

Another Claude session sent a message:
<teammate-message teammate_id="sol56-spec-review" color="yellow" summary="Diff review complete: NOT safe to merge — 1 major, 2 minors">
Sol56 diff review completed (PID 1872 exited clean, 121,405 tokens). Verdict: changes required before merge — one major functional gap, two minors, no blockers, no nits.

---

VERBATIM CODEX OUTPUT:

Verdict: changes required before merge. I found one major functional gap and two minors. No blockers or nits.

## Major

1. Unlabeled passthrough commands are parsed successfully but rejected server-side.

The amended grammar intentionally treats `claude --model=x` as an agent command, not `label=agent` (src/cli/team.rs:120), and the unit test confirms that interpretation (src/cli/team.rs:293).

However, when no label is provided, the server builds the label from the entire command:

```rust
format!("{}-{}", entry.agent, n)
```

(src/app/api/team.rs:83)

Thus `claude --model=x` becomes `claude --model=x-1`, which immediately fails the whitespace prohibition at src/app/api/team.rs:92. Other valid passthrough commands containing paths or whitespace fail similarly.

This leaves the documented agent-only passthrough form unusable unless the caller supplies an explicit label. Generate a safe default label from the command's executable/detected agent, or require an explicit label and amend the grammar/documentation accordingly.

## Minor

1. Default cwd is not always sent.

The CLI calls `current_dir()`, but converts failure to `None` using `.ok()` (src/cli/team.rs:101). In that case the wire request omits cwd and the server falls back to its own workspace-derived cwd (src/app/api/workspaces.rs:43), contrary to the binding "always sends cwd" amendment.

Propagate the `current_dir()` error instead of silently reverting to server inference.

2. The protocol-19 checklist missed `tests/cli_wrapper.rs`.

Production constants and the generated artifact are correctly at 19:
- src/protocol/wire.rs:16
- tests/support/mod.rs:18
- docs/next/api/herdr-api.schema.json:3

But six status-command assertions still expect protocol 18, starting at tests/cli_wrapper.rs:1705 and continuing through tests/cli_wrapper.rs:1779. This is concrete evidence that the focused-suite scope omitted part of the binding bump checklist; it is not a generic complaint about the deferred monolithic suite.

## Prior-finding verification

1. Reserved `all`: resolved. Exact server-side rejection occurs before creation at src/app/api/team.rs:63.

2. Pane-ID labels and normalization: resolved. Explicit labels are trimmed before validation and duplicate comparison at src/app/api/team.rs:83, with canonical pane-ID rejection at src/app/api/team.rs:99. The `msg.rs` change correctly only widens the canonical validator to `pub(crate)` for reuse (src/msg.rs:451).

3. Client-owned default cwd: partially resolved. Normal execution sends `current_dir()`, but the error path silently sends `None`.

4. Identifier-only roster grammar: partially resolved. Parsing ambiguity is fixed at src/cli/team.rs:120, but unlabeled passthrough commands can fail server label validation as described above.

5. Dual-signal readiness/full inventory: resolved. Eligibility uses the spawn result's expected roster agent plus the shared detector inventory at src/cli/team.rs:160; readiness uses live `PaneInfo.agent || agent_status != unknown` at src/cli/team.rs:197. The detector contains 21 agent variants at src/detect/mod.rs:43.

6. Focus-restoring rollback: resolved. `active` and `selected` are captured before creation and restored through the common failure path at src/app/api/team.rs:134 and src/app/api/team.rs:158.

7. 24-pane cap: resolved. The total includes the orchestrator pane and is rejected before creation at src/app/api/team.rs:71.

Config initialization and live reload are correctly wired at src/app/mod.rs:673 and src/app/mod.rs:1501. `git diff --check 93ffa86..923a8e0` is clean.

Merge verdict: not safe to merge as-is. Fix the passthrough auto-label behavior, make cwd resolution fail explicitly, and update the stale protocol assertions first.

---

MY SYNTHESIS:

5 of 7 prior spec-review findings are cleanly resolved (reserved "all", pane-ID label rejection, dual-signal readiness with full 21-agent inventory, focus-restoring rollback, 24-pane cap) — all with direct file:line verification against team.rs/cli/team.rs. 2 are only partially resolved, and both partial resolutions converge on the same root cause: the unlabeled-passthrough path.

The single major finding is concrete and actionable: when a roster entry has no explicit label, the server derives one via `format!("{}-{}", entry.agent, n)` using the *entire* command string as `entry.agent` (app/api/team.rs:83). For a bare registry name like `claude` this is fine, but for any passthrough command with flags or spaces — the exact case the amended grammar was redesigned to support — the generated label contains whitespace and immediately fails validation at app/api/team.rs:92. So the CLI parser accepts `claude --model=x` correctly, but the server then rejects it downstream. That's not a partial edge case; it makes the entire "identifier-only label=agent OR bare passthrough command" grammar unusable for the passthrough half unless the caller always supplies an explicit label — which defeats the point of having designed that form.

The two minors are smaller but real: cwd resolution failure silently degrades to server inference (contradicts the binding "always sends cwd" amendment) instead of surfacing an error, and 6 assertions in tests/cli_wrapper.rs still hardcode protocol 18 even though production code correctly bumped to 19 — Codex called out that this is concrete evidence the focused-suite scope missed part of the bump checklist, not a complaint about the deliberately-deferred monolithic suite.

Bottom line: this is a tight, well-targeted punch list — one server-side label-generation bug plus two small correctness fixes — not a redesign. All three are localized to app/api/team.rs, cli/team.rs, and the stale test assertions.

Sol56 closing verification completed (PID 956 exited clean, 131,655 tokens). Verdict: not yet ready to merge. 4f23c3b fixed 2 of 3 prior findings cleanly, but the passthrough-label fix is only partially complete — a narrower edge case in the same code path survived.

---

VERBATIM CODEX OUTPUT:

## Findings

Blocker: none.

Major:

- Passthrough executable parsing remains incomplete. src/app/api/team.rs:90 uses `split_whitespace()`, so quoted Windows paths are misidentified:
  - `"C:\tools\mytool.exe" --flag` → `mytoolexe-1`
  - `"C:\Program Files\mytool.exe" --flag` → `Program-1`
  - `& "C:\Program Files\mytool.exe" --flag` → `agent-1`

  Additionally, src/app/api/team.rs:98 strips only lowercase `.exe`; `MYTOOL.EXE` becomes `MYTOOLEXE-1`. This violates the executable-base requirement for common Windows command forms and can group unrelated `Program Files` executables under the same counter.

Minor:

- The regression test at src/app/api/team.rs:473 covers flags and one unquoted lowercase `.exe` path, but not:
  - quoted paths;
  - paths containing spaces;
  - uppercase/mixed-case `.EXE`;
  - two different commands sharing one executable, such as `claude --model=x` and `claude --model=y`.

## Prior findings

- (a) Passthrough auto-labels: partially resolved. Flags and unquoted full/relative `/` or `\` paths work. Counters correctly key off the derived base at src/app/api/team.rs:103, so ordinary `claude --model=x` / `claude --model=y` variants produce sequential labels. Quoted Windows paths and case-insensitive `.exe` handling remain incorrect.
- (b) cwd failure handling: resolved. src/cli/team.rs:101 now propagates `current_dir()` failure through `map_err`, producing parse-time exit 2 instead of omitting `cwd`.
- (c) Protocol-19 assertions: resolved. All six assertions now expect 19 at tests/cli_wrapper.rs:1705, lines 1738, 1750, 1760, 1774, and 1779. A repository search found no remaining protocol-18 constants/assertions.

`4f23c3b` otherwise introduces no additional correctness issue in its cwd or protocol hunks; its diff also passes `git diff --check`.

## Merge verdict

Not yet ready to merge. Fix the remaining passthrough executable-token handling and add the missing counter/path regression cases. Once addressed, the verdict can be ready to merge conditional on the already-documented healthy-machine suite gate.

---

MY SYNTHESIS:

(b) and (c) are cleanly closed — cwd failure now hard-errors at parse time via `map_err` (cli/team.rs:101), and all six stale protocol assertions in cli_wrapper.rs are confirmed at 19 with no repo-wide protocol-18 remnants. (a) is where the fix commit undershot: it correctly moved to deriving the label from the executable base name and fixed the counter-keying concern (`claude --model=x` / `claude --model=y` now get distinct sequential labels, e.g. `claude-1`/`claude-2`), which was the core of the original finding and is what got e2e-verified with `pwsh -NoLogo` → `pwsh-1`. But the new implementation uses `split_whitespace()` to find the executable token, which breaks on the specific Windows command shapes that contain spaces themselves: quoted paths (`"C:\tools\mytool.exe"`), and PowerShell's call-operator form (`& "C:\Program Files\mytool.exe"`). It also only strips lowercase `.exe`, so `MYTOOL.EXE` doesn't get its suffix trimmed. None of these are hypothetical — they're standard ways to invoke an executable with a path containing spaces on Windows, which is exactly the CLI-passthrough scenario this spec's whole roster-grammar redesign was for.

No blocker, one major (narrower in scope than the original — it's now a tokenization completeness gap, not a "the feature doesn't work" gap), one minor (test coverage should include the cases above once fixed). Codex's framing is fair: this is close, and it explicitly pre-approved the path to done — fix the tokenizer to handle quoted/spaced paths and case-insensitive `.exe`, add regression tests for those shapes, and the verdict becomes ready-to-merge conditional on the already-documented healthy-machine suite gate. No new engagement should be needed if that narrow fix lands; it's a same-function tweak, not a design change.
</teammate-message>

--- ASSISTANT [2026-07-19T07:42:15.307Z] ---
Because of what today's session did to Windows' console infrastructure, and the fact that there's no way to repair it short of a restart:

**The symptom set.** Over the session we saw four things with one shared signature: your `0xC0000142` errors ("DLL initialization failed" — the classic code for a *process failing to start*), my background shells getting killed, herdrplus silently dying between e2e runs, and test suites freezing at random-but-always-child-spawning tests (git worktree creation, PTY/ConPTY spawns) while each of those tests passes fine in isolation. The tests hang rather than fail because they block in unbounded waits for a "child started" event that never arrives when the spawn itself dies.

**The cause.** This session spawned and killed an unusually large number of processes and consoles — dozens of herdr panes with shells, multiple full test suites (each spawning hundreds of short-lived PTYs), zig builds, worker agents, and a lot of force-kills. That churn exhausts and fragments kernel-side per-session resources — desktop heap and console/ConPTY session objects. Those pools don't show up in Task Manager, aren't tied to any live process I can kill (I checked: zero orphans by parent-liveness), and Windows has no mechanism to compact or reclaim them while the session is up. A reboot is simply the only reset button that pool has.

**The honest caveat:** it's degradation, not a hard failure — spawns still succeed *most* of the time (the e2e passed, builds completed). So you don't strictly *have* to reboot: you could just run the single-threaded gate as-is and it might get through on a good roll, or after the machine has been quiet for a while. Reboot is the reliable path, not the only one. If you'd like, I can fire the gate right now in a herdr pane and we see how far it gets — worst case it hangs at some spawn again and the reboot recommendation stands.
